</tr><tr><td style="padding:0 0.1em 0.4em">

</tr><tr><td style="text-align:right;font-size:115%;padding-top: 0.6em;"><div class="plainlinks hlist navbar mini"><ul><li class="nv-view"><a href="/wiki/Template:Green_politics" title="Template:Green politics"><abbr title="View this template">v</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-talk"><a href="/wiki/Template_talk:Green_politics" title="Template talk:Green politics"><abbr title="Discuss this template">t</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-edit"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:Green_politics&amp;action=edit"><abbr title="Edit this template">e</abbr></a></li></ul></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><b>The Green Party of England and Wales</b> (<b>GPEW</b>; <a href="/wiki/Welsh_language" title="Welsh language">Welsh</a>: <i lang="cy">Plaid Werdd Cymru a Lloegr</i>) is a <a href="/wiki/Green_politics" title="Green politics">green</a>, <a href="/wiki/Left-wing_politics" title="Left-wing politics">left-wing</a> <a href="/wiki/List_of_political_parties_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="List of political parties in the United Kingdom">political party in England and Wales</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-independent.co.uk_7-1"><a href="#cite_note-independent.co.uk-7">[7]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EUROPP_8-1"><a href="#cite_note-EUROPP-8">[8]</a></sup> Headquartered in <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a>, since September 2018, its Co-Leaders are <a href="/wiki/Si%C3%A2n_Berry" title="Siân Berry">Siân Berry</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jonathan_Bartley" title="Jonathan Bartley">Jonathan Bartley</a>. The Green Party has one <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Member_of_Parliament" title="Member of Parliament">Member of Parliament</a> in the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Commons_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="House of Commons of the United Kingdom">House of Commons</a>, one representative in the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Lords" title="House of Lords">House of Lords</a>, and three <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Members_of_the_European_Parliament" title="Members of the European Parliament">Members of the European Parliament</a>. It has various councillors in <a href="/wiki/Local_government_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="Local government in the United Kingdom">UK local government</a> and two members of the <a href="/wiki/London_Assembly" title="London Assembly">London Assembly</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gwydir_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-gwydir-12">[12]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Elections_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-Elections-13">[13]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-brumpost_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-brumpost-14">[14]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-solihull_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-solihull-15">[15]</a></sup>
</p><p>The party's ideology combines <a href="/wiki/Environmentalism" title="Environmentalism">environmentalism</a> with left-wing economic policies, including well-funded, locally controlled public services within the confines of a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Steady_state_economy" title="Steady state economy">steady state economy</a>, and it supports <a href="/wiki/Proportional_representation" title="Proportional representation">proportional representation</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> It also takes a <a href="/wiki/Progressivism#Contemporary_mainstream_political_conception" title="Progressivism">progressive</a> approach to social policies such as <a href="/wiki/Civil_liberties" title="Civil liberties">civil liberties</a>, <a href="/wiki/Animal_rights" title="Animal rights">animal rights</a>, <a href="/wiki/LGBT_rights_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="LGBT rights in the United Kingdom">LGBT rights</a> and <a href="/wiki/Drug_policy_reform" title="Drug policy reform">drug policy reform</a>. The party also believes strongly in <a href="/wiki/Nonviolence" title="Nonviolence">nonviolence</a>, <a href="/wiki/Basic_income" title="Basic income">basic income</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Living_wage" title="Living wage">living wage</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-£10_Minimum_Wage_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-£10_Minimum_Wage-17">[17]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Democracy" title="Democracy">democratic</a> participation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CoreValues_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-CoreValues-18">[18]</a></sup> The party comprises various regional divisions, including the semi-autonomous <a href="/wiki/Wales_Green_Party" title="Wales Green Party">Wales Green Party</a>. Internationally, the party is affiliated to the <a href="/wiki/Global_Greens" title="Global Greens">Global Greens</a> and the <a href="/wiki/European_Green_Party" title="European Green Party">European Green Party</a>.
</p><p>The Green Party of England and Wales was established in 1990 alongside the <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Green_Party" title="Scottish Green Party">Scottish Green Party</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Green_Party_in_Northern_Ireland" title="Green Party in Northern Ireland">Green Party in Northern Ireland</a> through the division of the pre-existing <a href="/wiki/Green_Party_(UK)" title="Green Party (UK)">Green Party</a>, a group which had originally been established as the <a href="/wiki/PEOPLE_Party" title="PEOPLE Party">PEOPLE Party</a> in 1973. Experiencing centralising reforms spearheaded by the <a href="/wiki/Green_2000" title="Green 2000">Green 2000</a> group in the early 1990s, the party sought to emphasise growth in local governance, doing so throughout the 1990s. In 2010, the party gained its first MP in Lucas, who represents the constituency of <a href="/wiki/Brighton_Pavilion_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="Brighton Pavilion (UK Parliament constituency)">Brighton Pavilion</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBC-election2010-brightonpavillion_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-BBC-election2010-brightonpavillion-19">[19]</a></sup>
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Green_Party_of_England_and_Wales&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Green_Party_of_England_and_Wales" title="History of the Green Party of England and Wales">History of the Green Party of England and Wales</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Origins">Origins</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Green_Party_of_England_and_Wales&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Origins">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The Green Party of England and Wales has its origins in the <a href="/wiki/PEOPLE_Party" title="PEOPLE Party">PEOPLE Party</a>, which was founded in <a href="/wiki/Coventry" title="Coventry">Coventry</a> in 1973.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERootes199566Birch200954_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERootes199566Birch200954-20">[20]</a></sup> PEOPLE was renamed <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Ecology_Party" title="The Ecology Party">The Ecology Party</a> in 1975,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERootes199566Birch200954_20-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERootes199566Birch200954-20">[20]</a></sup> and in 1985 changed again to the <a href="/wiki/Green_Party_(UK)" title="Green Party (UK)">Green Party</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcCulloch1992421Birch200954_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcCulloch1992421Birch200954-21">[21]</a></sup> In 1989 the party's Scottish branch split to establish the independent <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Green_Party" title="Scottish Green Party">Scottish Green Party</a>, with an independent <a href="/wiki/Green_Party_in_Northern_Ireland" title="Green Party in Northern Ireland">Green Party in Northern Ireland</a> developing shortly after, leaving those branches in England and Wales to form their own party.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBirch200954_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBirch200954-22">[22]</a></sup> The Green Party of England and Wales is registered with the <a href="/wiki/Electoral_Commission_(United_Kingdom)" title="Electoral Commission (United Kingdom)">Electoral Commission</a> as simply the Green Party.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ECregister_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-ECregister-23">[23]</a></sup>
</p><p>In the <a href="/wiki/European_Parliament_election,_1989_(United_Kingdom)" title="European Parliament election, 1989 (United Kingdom)">1989 European Parliament elections</a>, the Green Party of England and Wales polled 15% of the vote with 2.3 million votes, the best ever performance of a Green party in a nationwide election.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPattieRussellJohnston1991286McCulloch1992422Rootes199568&amp;ndash;69Burchell2000145Birch200954_24-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPattieRussellJohnston1991286McCulloch1992422Rootes199568&amp;ndash;69Burchell2000145Birch200954-24">[24]</a></sup> This gave it the third largest share of the vote after the <a href="/wiki/Conservative_Party_(UK)" title="Conservative Party (UK)">Conservative</a> and <a href="/wiki/Labour_Party_(UK)" title="Labour Party (UK)">Labour</a> parties, although because of the <a href="/wiki/First-past-the-post_voting" title="First-past-the-post voting">first-past-the-post voting</a> system it failed to gain a <a href="/wiki/Member_of_the_European_Parliament" title="Member of the European Parliament">Member of the European Parliament</a> (MEP).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPattieRussellJohnston1991286Birch200954_25-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPattieRussellJohnston1991286Birch200954-25">[25]</a></sup> This success has been attributed to both the increased respectability of environmentalism and the effects of the development boom in southern England in the late 1980s.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERootes199569&amp;ndash;72_26-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERootes199569&amp;ndash;72-26">[26]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Early_years:_1990.E2.80.932008"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_years:_1990–2008">Early years: 1990–2008</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Green_Party_of_England_and_Wales&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Early years: 1990–2008">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Seeking to capitalise on the Greens' success in the EP elections, a group named <a href="/wiki/Green_2000" title="Green 2000">Green 2000</a> was established in July 1990, arguing for an internal reorganisation of the party in order to develop it into an effective electoral force capable of securing seats in the House of Commons.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcCulloch1992422Burchell2000145_27-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcCulloch1992422Burchell2000145-27">[27]</a></sup> Its proposed reforms included a more centralised structure, the replacement of the existing party council with a smaller party executive, and the establishment of delegate voting at party conferences.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBurchell2000145_28-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBurchell2000145-28">[28]</a></sup> Many party members opposed the reforms, believing that they would undermine the internal party democracy, and amid the arguments various key members resigned or were dismissed from the Greens.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBurchell2000145&amp;ndash;146_29-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBurchell2000145&amp;ndash;146-29">[29]</a></sup> Although Green 2000 proposals were defeated at the party's 1990 conference, they were overwhelmingly carried at their 1991 conference, resulting in an internal restructuring of the party.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcCulloch1992422_30-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcCulloch1992422-30">[30]</a></sup> Between the end of 1990 and mid-1992, the party lost over half its members, with those polled indicating that frustration over a lack of clear and effective party leadership was a major reason in their decision.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBirch200968_31-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBirch200968-31">[31]</a></sup> The party fielded more candidates than it had ever done before in the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_general_election,_1992" title="United Kingdom general election, 1992">1992 general election</a> but was widely deemed to have performed poorly.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERootes199575_32-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERootes199575-32">[32]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1993, the party adopted its "Basis for Renewal" program in an attempt to bring together conflicting factions and thus save the party from bankruptcy and potential demise.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBurchell2000146_33-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBurchell2000146-33">[33]</a></sup> The party sought to escape their reputation as an environmentalist <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Single-issue_party" title="Single-issue party">single-issue party</a> by placing greater emphasis on social policies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBurchell2000148_34-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBurchell2000148-34">[34]</a></sup>
Recognising their poor performance in the 1992 national elections, the party decided to focus on gaining support in local elections, targeting wards where there was a pre-existing support base of Green activists.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBurchell2000146_33-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBurchell2000146-33">[33]</a></sup> In 1993, future party leader and MP Lucas gained a seat on <a href="/wiki/Oxfordshire_County_Council" title="Oxfordshire County Council">Oxfordshire County Council</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERootes199579Burchell2000146_35-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERootes199579Burchell2000146-35">[35]</a></sup> with other gains following in the 1995 and 1996 local elections.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBurchell2000146_33-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBurchell2000146-33">[33]</a></sup>
</p><p>The Greens sought to build alliances with other parties in the hope of gaining representation at the parliamentary level.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBurchell2000147_36-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBurchell2000147-36">[36]</a></sup> In Wales, the Greens endorsed <a href="/wiki/Plaid_Cymru" title="Plaid Cymru">Plaid Cymru</a> candidate <a href="/wiki/Cynog_Dafis" title="Cynog Dafis">Cynog Dafis</a> in the 1992 general election, having worked with him on a number of environmental initiatives.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBurchell2000147_36-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBurchell2000147-36">[36]</a></sup> For the 1997 general election, the Ceredigion branch of the Greens endorsed Dafis as a joint Plaid Cymru/Green candidate, but this generated controversy with the party, with critics believing it improper to build an alliance with a party that did not share all of the Greens' views. In April 1995 the Green National Executive ruled that the party should withdraw from this alliance due to ideological differences.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBurchell2000147_36-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBurchell2000147-36">[36]</a></sup>
</p><p>As the Labour Party shifted to the political centre under the leadership of <a href="/wiki/Tony_Blair" title="Tony Blair">Tony Blair</a> and his <a href="/wiki/New_Labour" title="New Labour">New Labour</a> project, the Greens sought to gain the support of the party's dissafected leftists.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBirch200955_37-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBirch200955-37">[37]</a></sup>
During the <a href="/wiki/European_Parliament_election,_1999_(United_Kingdom)" title="European Parliament election, 1999 (United Kingdom)">1999 European Parliament elections</a>, the first to be held in the UK using <a href="/wiki/Proportional_representation" title="Proportional representation">proportional representation</a>, the Greens gained their first Members of the European Parliament (MEPs), Lucas (<a href="/wiki/South_East_England_(European_Parliament_constituency)" title="South East England (European Parliament constituency)">South East England</a>) and <a href="/wiki/Jean_Lambert" title="Jean Lambert">Jean Lambert</a> (<a href="/wiki/London_(European_Parliament_constituency)" title="London (European Parliament constituency)">London</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBurchell2000145,_149_38-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBurchell2000145,_149-38">[38]</a></sup> At the <a href="/wiki/London_Assembly_election,_2000" title="London Assembly election, 2000">inaugural London Assembly Elections in 2000</a>, the party gained 11% of the vote and returned three <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Members_of_the_London_Assembly" title="Members of the London Assembly">Assembly Members</a> (AM),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBurchell2000149&amp;ndash;150Birch200955_39-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBurchell2000149&amp;ndash;150Birch200955-39">[39]</a></sup> and although this dropped to two following the <a href="/wiki/London_Assembly_election,_2004" title="London Assembly election, 2004">2004 London Assembly Elections</a>, the Green AMs proved vital in passing the annual budget of Mayor <a href="/wiki/Ken_Livingstone" title="Ken Livingstone">Ken Livingstone</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBirch200955_37-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBirch200955-37">[37]</a></sup>
</p><p>At the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_general_election,_2001" title="United Kingdom general election, 2001">2001 general election</a> they polled 0.7% of the vote and gained no seats.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup> At the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/European_Parliament_Election,_2004_(United_Kingdom)" title="European Parliament Election, 2004 (United Kingdom)">2004 European Parliamentary elections</a> the party returned 2 MEPS the same as in 1999; overall, the Party polled 1,033,093 votes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup> In the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_general_election,_2005" title="United Kingdom general election, 2005">2005 general election</a> the party gained over 1% of the vote for the first time, and polled over 10% in the constituencies of <a href="/wiki/Brighton_Pavilion_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="Brighton Pavilion (UK Parliament constituency)">Brighton Pavilion</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lewisham_Deptford_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="Lewisham Deptford (UK Parliament constituency)">Lewisham Deptford</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBirch200956_42-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBirch200956-42">[42]</a></sup> This growth has been attributed to the increasing public visibility of the party as well as a general growth in support for smaller parties in the UK.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBirch200956_42-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBirch200956-42">[42]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Caroline_Lucas_.282008.E2.80.9312.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Caroline_Lucas_(2008–12)">Caroline Lucas (2008–12)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Green_Party_of_England_and_Wales&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Caroline Lucas (2008–12)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><div class="PopUpMediaTransform" id="mwe_player_0" style="width:220px;" videopayload='&lt;div class="mediaContainer" style="width:640px"&gt;&lt;video id="mwe_player_1" poster="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Caroline_Lucas_speech_20080906.ogv/640px--Caroline_Lucas_speech_20080906.ogv.jpg" controls="" preload="none" autoplay="" style="width:640px;height:480px" class="kskin" data-durationhint="25.033381712627" data-startoffset="0" data-mwtitle="Caroline_Lucas_speech_20080906.ogv" data-mwprovider="wikimediacommons"&gt;&lt;source src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/transcoded/5/5f/Caroline_Lucas_speech_20080906.ogv/Caroline_Lucas_speech_20080906.ogv.480p.vp9.webm" type="video/webm; codecs=&amp;quot;vp8, vorbis&amp;quot;" data-title="WebM (360P)" data-shorttitle="WebM 360P" data-transcodekey="360p.webm" data-width="480" data-height="360" data-bandwidth="541568" data-framerate="30.000300003"/&gt;&lt;/video&gt;&lt;/div&gt;'><img alt="File:Caroline Lucas speech 20080906.ogv" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Caroline_Lucas_speech_20080906.ogv/220px--Caroline_Lucas_speech_20080906.ogv.jpg" style="width:220px;height:165px"/><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/5/5f/Caroline_Lucas_speech_20080906.ogv" target="new" title="Play media"><span class="play-btn-large"><span class="mw-tmh-playtext">Play media</span></span></a></div> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Caroline_Lucas_speech_20080906.ogv" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Lucas speaking as the first Leader of the Green Party of England and Wales at its autumn conference in 2008.</div></div></div>
<p>In November 2007, the party held an internal referendum to decide on whether it should replace its use of two "principal speakers", one male and the other female, with the more conventional roles of "leader" and "deputy leader"; the motion passed with 73% of the vote.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBirch200967_43-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBirch200967-43">[43]</a></sup> In September 2008, the party then elected its first leader, Lucas,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBirch200967_43-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBirch200967-43">[43]</a></sup> with <a href="/wiki/Adrian_Ramsay" title="Adrian Ramsay">Adrian Ramsay</a> elected deputy leader.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup> In the party's first election with Lucas as leader, it retained both its MEPs in the <a href="/wiki/European_Parliament_election,_2009_(United_Kingdom)" title="European Parliament election, 2009 (United Kingdom)">2009 European elections</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup>
</p><p>In the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_general_election_2010" title="United Kingdom general election 2010">2010 general election</a>, the party returned its first <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Member_of_Parliament#United_Kingdom" title="Member of Parliament">Member of Parliament</a> (MP). Lucas was returned as MP for the seat of <a href="/wiki/Brighton_Pavilion_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="Brighton Pavilion (UK Parliament constituency)">Brighton Pavilion</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup> Following the election, <a href="/wiki/Keith_Taylor_(British_politician)" title="Keith Taylor (British politician)">Keith Taylor</a> succeeded her as MEP for South East England. They also saved their deposit in <a href="/wiki/Hove_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="Hove (UK Parliament constituency)">Hove</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Brighton_Kemptown_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="Brighton Kemptown (UK Parliament constituency)">Brighton Kemptown</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup>
</p><p>In the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_local_elections,_2011" title="United Kingdom local elections, 2011">2011 local government elections in England and Wales</a>, the Green Party in Brighton and Hove took minority control of the <a href="/wiki/Brighton_and_Hove_City_Council" title="Brighton and Hove City Council">City Council</a> by winning 23 seats, 5 short of an overall majority.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p><p>At the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_local_elections,_2012" title="United Kingdom local elections, 2012">2012 local government elections</a> the Green Party gained 5 seats, and retained both AMs at the <a href="/wiki/London_Assembly_election,_2012" title="London Assembly election, 2012">2012 London Assembly election</a>. At the <a href="/wiki/London_mayoral_election,_2012" title="London mayoral election, 2012">London Mayoral Election</a> the party's candidate <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jenny_Jones_(Green_politician)" title="Jenny Jones (Green politician)">Jenny Jones</a> finished third, and lost her deposit.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p><p>In May 2012, Lucas announced that she would not seek re-election to the post of party leader.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup> In September, <a href="/wiki/Natalie_Bennett" title="Natalie Bennett">Natalie Bennett</a> was elected party leader and <a href="/wiki/Will_Duckworth" title="Will Duckworth">Will Duckworth</a> deputy leader in the <a href="/wiki/Green_Party_of_England_and_Wales_leadership_election,_2012" title="Green Party of England and Wales leadership election, 2012">leadership election took place</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-new_leader_49-0"><a href="#cite_note-new_leader-49">[49]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Guardian_new_leader_50-0"><a href="#cite_note-Guardian_new_leader-50">[50]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Natalie_Bennett_.282012.E2.80.9316.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Natalie_Bennett_(2012–16)">Natalie Bennett (2012–16)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Green_Party_of_England_and_Wales&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Natalie Bennett (2012–16)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_local_elections,_2013" title="United Kingdom local elections, 2013">2013 local government elections</a> saw overall gains of 5 seats. The Party returned representation for the first time on the councils of Cornwall, Devon, and Essex.
</p><p>At the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_local_elections,_2014" title="United Kingdom local elections, 2014">local government elections the following year</a>, the Greens gained 18 seats overall.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> In London, the party won four seats, a gain of two, holding seats in <a href="/wiki/London_Borough_of_Camden" title="London Borough of Camden">Camden</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/London_Borough_of_Lewisham" title="London Borough of Lewisham">Lewisham</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup> and gaining seats in <a href="/wiki/London_Borough_of_Islington" title="London Borough of Islington">Islington</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/London_Borough_of_Lambeth" title="London Borough of Lambeth">Lambeth</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup>
</p>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r856303569">@media all and (max-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .tmulti>.thumbinner{width:100%!important;max-width:none!important}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{float:none!important;max-width:none!important;width:100%!important;text-align:center}}</style><div class="thumb tmulti tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:353px;max-width:353px"><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:147px;max-width:147px"><div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Amelia_womack.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="1672" data-file-width="1298" height="187" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Amelia_womack.jpg/145px-Amelia_womack.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Amelia_womack.jpg/218px-Amelia_womack.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Amelia_womack.jpg/290px-Amelia_womack.jpg 2x" width="145"/></a></div></div><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px"><div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Shahrah_ali.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="672" data-file-width="744" height="181" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Shahrah_ali.jpg/200px-Shahrah_ali.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Shahrah_ali.jpg/300px-Shahrah_ali.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Shahrah_ali.jpg/400px-Shahrah_ali.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a></div></div><div style="clear:left"></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left;text-align:left;background-color:transparent"><a href="/wiki/Amelia_Womack" title="Amelia Womack">Womack</a> and <a href="/wiki/Shahrar_Ali" title="Shahrar Ali">Ali</a> were voted deputy leaders in 2014</div></div></div>
<p>At the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/European_Parliament_Election,_2014_(United_Kingdom)" title="European Parliament Election, 2014 (United Kingdom)">2014 European elections</a> The Green Party finished fourth, above the <a href="/wiki/Liberal_Democrats_(UK)" title="Liberal Democrats (UK)">Liberal Democrats</a>, winning over 1.2 million votes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup> The party increased its European Parliament representation, gaining one seat in the <a href="/wiki/South_West_England_(European_Parliament_constituency)" title="South West England (European Parliament constituency)">South West England</a> region.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup>
</p><p>In September 2014, The Green Party held its biennial leadership elections. Incumbent leader Bennett ran uncontested, and retained her status as party leader. The election also saw a change in the elective format for position of deputy leader. The party opted to elect two, gender-balanced deputy leaders, instead of one. <a href="/wiki/Amelia_Womack" title="Amelia Womack">Amelia Womack</a> and <a href="/wiki/Shahrar_Ali" title="Shahrar Ali">Shahrar Ali</a> won the two positions, succeeding former deputy leader Duckworth.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Identifying_reliable_sources" title="Wikipedia:Identifying reliable sources"><span title="The material near this tag relies on an unreliable source. Self-published source (blog) (May 2015)">unreliable source</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p><p>The party announced in October 2014 that Green candidates would be standing for parliament in at least 75% of constituencies in the 2015 general election. In the 2010 general election, they contested roughly 50% of seats.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup> Following its rapid increase in membership and support, the Green Party also announced it was targeting twelve key seats for the 2015 general election. These seats were its one current seat, <a href="/wiki/Brighton_Pavilion_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="Brighton Pavilion (UK Parliament constituency)">Brighton Pavilion</a>, held by Lucas since 2010; <a href="/wiki/Norwich_South_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="Norwich South (UK Parliament constituency)">Norwich South</a>, a Liberal Democrat seat where June 2014 polling put the Greens in second place behind Labour;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Bristol_West_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="Bristol West (UK Parliament constituency)">Bristol West</a>, another Liberal Democrat seat, where they targeted the student vote; <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/St._Ives_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="St. Ives (UK Parliament constituency)">St. Ives</a>, where they received an average of 18% of the vote in county elections; <a href="/wiki/Sheffield_Central_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="Sheffield Central (UK Parliament constituency)">Sheffield Central</a>; <a href="/wiki/Liverpool_Riverside_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="Liverpool Riverside (UK Parliament constituency)">Liverpool Riverside</a>; <a href="/wiki/Oxford_East_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="Oxford East (UK Parliament constituency)">Oxford East</a>; <a href="/wiki/Solihull_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="Solihull (UK Parliament constituency)">Solihull</a>; <a href="/wiki/Reading_East_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="Reading East (UK Parliament constituency)">Reading East</a>; and three more seats with high student populations - <a href="/wiki/York_Central_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="York Central (UK Parliament constituency)">York Central</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cambridge_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="Cambridge (UK Parliament constituency)">Cambridge</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Holborn_and_St._Pancras_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="Holborn and St. Pancras (UK Parliament constituency)">Holborn and St. Pancras</a>, where leader Bennett stood as the candidate.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup>
</p><p>In December 2014, The Green Party announced that it had more than doubled its overall membership from 1 January that year to 30,809.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twitter.com_63-0"><a href="#cite_note-twitter.com-63">[63]</a></sup> This reflected the increase seen in opinion polls in 2014, with Green Party voting intentions trebling from 2-3% at the start of the year, to 7-8% at the end of the year, on many occasions, coming in fourth place with <a href="/wiki/YouGov" title="YouGov">YouGov</a>'s national polls, ahead of the Liberal Democrats, and gaining over 25% of the vote with 18 to 24-year-olds.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup> This rapid increase in support for the party is referred to by media as the "Green Surge".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup> The hashtag "#GreenSurge" has also been popular on social media (such as Twitter) from Green Party members and supporters,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup> and as of 15 January 2015<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Green_Party_of_England_and_Wales&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, the combined Green Party membership in the UK stood at 44,713; greater than the number of members of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UKIP" title="UKIP">UKIP</a> (at 41,943), and the <a href="/wiki/Liberal_Democrats_(UK)" title="Liberal Democrats (UK)">Liberal Democrats</a> (at 44,576).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup>
</p><p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Opinion_polling_for_the_2015_United_Kingdom_general_election" title="Opinion polling for the 2015 United Kingdom general election">Polling</a> subsequently fell back as the 2015 general election approached:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup> a Press Association poll of polls on 3 April, for example, put the Greens fifth with 5.4%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup> However, membership statistics continued to surge with the party attaining 60,000 in England and Wales that April.
</p><p>In the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_general_election,_2015" title="United Kingdom general election, 2015">2015 general election</a>, Lucas was re-elected in Brighton Pavilion with an increased majority, and while failing to gain any additional seats, the Greens received their highest-ever vote share (over 1.1 million votes), and increased their national share of the vote from 1% to 3.8%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup> Overnight, the membership numbers increased to over 63,000.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup> However they lost 9 out of their 20 seats on the Brighton and Hove council, losing minority control.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup> Nationwide, the Greens increased their share of councillors, gaining an additional 10 council seats while failing to gain overall control of any individual council.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup>
</p><p>On 15 May 2016 Bennett announced she would not be standing for re-election in the party's biennial <a href="/wiki/Green_Party_of_England_and_Wales_leadership_election,_2016" title="Green Party of England and Wales leadership election, 2016">leadership election</a> due to take place in the summer.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup> Former leader Lucas and Work and Pensions Spokesperson Bartley announced two weeks later that they intended to stand for leadership as a <a href="/wiki/Job_sharing" title="Job sharing">job share</a> arrangement.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-job_share_78-0"><a href="#cite_note-job_share-78">[78]</a></sup> Nominations closed at the end of June, with the campaign period taking place in July and voting period in August and the results announced at the party's Autumn Conference in Birmingham from 2–4 September. It was announced on 4 September that Lucas and Bartley would become the party's leaders in a job share.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Lucas_and_Bartley_.282016.E2.80.938.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Lucas_and_Bartley_(2016–8)">Lucas and Bartley (2016–8)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Green_Party_of_England_and_Wales&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Lucas and Bartley (2016–8)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Lucas first suggested "progressive pacts" to work on a number of issues including combating climate change and for electoral reform, following the results of the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_general_election,_2015" title="United Kingdom general election, 2015">2015 general election</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup> She then reiterated the call alongside Bartley as they announced their plan to share the leadership of the party.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-job_share_78-1"><a href="#cite_note-job_share-78">[78]</a></sup> Following the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_European_Union_membership_referendum,_2016" title="United Kingdom European Union membership referendum, 2016">vote to leave</a> the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> in June 2016, Bennett published an open letter, calling for an "anti-Brexit alliance" potentially comprising <a href="/wiki/Labour_Party_(UK)" title="Labour Party (UK)">Labour</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Liberal_Democrats_(UK)" title="Liberal Democrats (UK)">Liberal Democrats</a> and <a href="/wiki/Plaid_Cymru" title="Plaid Cymru">Plaid Cymru</a> to stand in a future <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_general_election,_2017" title="United Kingdom general election, 2017">snap election</a> in English and Welsh seats.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup> On 30 May 2018 Lucas announced she would not seek re-election in the <a href="/wiki/Green_Party_of_England_and_Wales_leadership_election,_2018" title="Green Party of England and Wales leadership election, 2018">Green Party of England and Wales leadership election, 2018</a>, and would stand down as co-leader.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup> On 1 June 2018 Bartley announced a co-leadership bid alongside <a href="/wiki/Si%C3%A2n_Berry" title="Siân Berry">Siân Berry</a>, former candidate for the Mayor of London in 2008 and 2016.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Ideology_and_policy">Ideology and policy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Green_Party_of_England_and_Wales&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Ideology and policy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Welfare_Not_Warfare.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1019" data-file-width="1071" height="209" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Welfare_Not_Warfare.jpg/220px-Welfare_Not_Warfare.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Welfare_Not_Warfare.jpg/330px-Welfare_Not_Warfare.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Welfare_Not_Warfare.jpg/440px-Welfare_Not_Warfare.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Welfare_Not_Warfare.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>"Welfare not Warfare" sign, indicating the Green Party's policy towards social justice and non-violence</div></div></div>
<p>Sociologist Chris Rootes stated that the Green Party took "the left-libertarian" vote,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERootes199576_84-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERootes199576-84">[84]</a></sup> while Dennison and Goodwin characterised it as reflecting "libertarian-universalistic values".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDennisonGoodwin2015185_85-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDennisonGoodwin2015185-85">[85]</a></sup> The party wants an end to "<a href="/wiki/Big_government" title="Big government">big government</a>" – which they see as hindering open and transparent democracy – and want to limit the power of "<a href="/wiki/Big_business" title="Big business">big business</a>" – which, they argue, upholds the unsustainable trend of globalisation, and is detrimental to local trade and economies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gydg_86-0"><a href="#cite_note-gydg-86">[86]</a></sup> There have been allegations of factionalism and infighting in the Green Party, between liberal, socialist, and anarchist factions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup>
</p><p>The Party publishes a full set of its policies, as approved by successive party conferences,collectively entitled "<i>Policies for a Sustainable Society</i>" (originally "<i>The Manifesto for a Sustainable Society</i>" before February 2010).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pss_88-0"><a href="#cite_note-pss-88">[88]</a></sup> This manifesto was summarised by <a href="/wiki/LGBT" title="LGBT">LGBT</a> and human rights campaigner <a href="/wiki/Peter_Tatchell" title="Peter Tatchell">Peter Tatchell</a> as "radical socialist", "incorporat[ing] key socialist values" as it "rejects privatisation, free market economics and globalisation, and includes commitments to public ownership, workers' rights, economic democracy, progressive taxation and the redistribution of wealth and power".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template noprint Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:No_original_research#Primary,_secondary_and_tertiary_sources" title="Wikipedia:No original research"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable secondary sources. (May 2018)">non-primary source needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Core_values">Core values</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Green_Party_of_England_and_Wales&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Core values">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Primary_sources" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg"><img alt="Question book-new.svg" data-file-height="399" data-file-width="512" height="39" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" width="50"/></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This article <b>relies too much on <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">references</a> to <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:No_original_research#Primary,_secondary_and_tertiary_sources" title="Wikipedia:No original research">primary sources</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please improve this  by adding <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:No_original_research#Primary,_secondary_and_tertiary_sources" title="Wikipedia:No original research">secondary or tertiary sources</a>.</span> <small><i>(May 2018)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>The ten core values set out by the Green Party policy document in February 2015<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Green_Party_of_England_and_Wales&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup> can be summarised as follows:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CoreValues_18-1"><a href="#cite_note-CoreValues-18">[18]</a></sup>
</p>
<ol><li>Commitment to <a href="/wiki/Social_justice" title="Social justice">social justice</a> and <a href="/wiki/Environmentalism" title="Environmentalism">environmentalism</a>, supporting a "radical transformation of society for the benefit of all, and for the planet as a whole". The threats to economic, social and environmental wellbeing are considered "part of the same problem", and "solving one of these crises cannot be achieved without solving the others."</li>
<li>Preservation of other species, because the human race "depends on the <a href="/wiki/Biodiversity" title="Biodiversity">diversity of the natural world</a> for its existence".</li>
<li>"A <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sustainable" title="Sustainable">sustainable</a> society" to guarantee humanity's long-term future, given that physical resources are <a href="/wiki/Non-renewable_resource" title="Non-renewable resource">finite</a>.</li>
<li>"Basic material security" as a universal, permanent entitlement.</li>
<li>Actions to "take account of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wellbeing" title="Wellbeing">wellbeing</a> of other nations, other species, and future generations", not advancing "our well-being to the detriment of theirs".</li>
<li>"<a href="/wiki/Voluntaryism" title="Voluntaryism">Voluntary co-operation</a> between empowered individuals in a democratic society, free from <a href="/wiki/Discrimination" title="Discrimination">discrimination</a> whether based on race, colour, gender, sexual orientation, religion, social origin or any other <a href="/wiki/Prejudice" title="Prejudice">prejudice</a>", as the basis of a "healthy society".</li>
<li>Decisions to be made "at the <a href="/wiki/Localism_(politics)" title="Localism (politics)">closest practical level</a> to those affected by them" to "emphasise democratic participation and <a href="/wiki/Accountability" title="Accountability">accountability</a>".</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Non-violent" title="Non-violent">Non-violent</a> solutions to conflict, seeking lasting settlement, taking into account "the interests of <a href="/wiki/Minority_group" title="Minority group">minorities</a> and future generations".</li>
<li>End the use of "narrow <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Economic_indicators" title="Economic indicators">economic indicators</a>" to measure society's success. Instead "take account of factors affecting the <a href="/wiki/Quality_of_life" title="Quality of life">quality of life</a> for all people: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Personal_freedom" title="Personal freedom">personal freedom</a>, <a href="/wiki/Social_equity" title="Social equity">social equity</a>, health, happiness and human fulfilment".</li>
<li>Use "a variety of methods, including lifestyle changes, to help effect progress", in addition to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Electoral_politics" title="Electoral politics">electoral politics</a>.</li></ol>
<p>The party also has a much larger and broader "philosophical basis", which covers many of these areas in more detail.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Manifesto">Manifesto</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Green_Party_of_England_and_Wales&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Manifesto">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Update" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><img alt="Ambox current red.svg" data-file-height="290" data-file-width="360" height="34" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Ambox_current_red.svg/42px-Ambox_current_red.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Ambox_current_red.svg/63px-Ambox_current_red.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Ambox_current_red.svg/84px-Ambox_current_red.svg.png 2x" width="42"/></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section needs to be <b>updated</b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please update this article to reflect recent events or newly available information.</span> <small><i>(May 2018)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>The party publishes a manifesto for each of its election campaigns.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pss_88-1"><a href="#cite_note-pss-88">[88]</a></sup> In their 2015 Election Manifesto, for the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_general_election,_2015" title="United Kingdom general election, 2015">2015 general election</a>, the Greens outlined many new policies, including a <a href="/wiki/Robin_Hood_tax" title="Robin Hood tax"><i>Robin Hood</i> tax</a> on banks, and a new 60% tax on those earning over £150,000.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup>
</p><p>The party also states that it would phase out <a href="/wiki/Fossil_fuel" title="Fossil fuel">fossil fuel</a>-based power generation, and would close all coal-fired power stations by 2023. The Green Party would also phase out nuclear power within ten years.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_policy_and_defence">Foreign policy and defence</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Green_Party_of_England_and_Wales&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Foreign policy and defence">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Since at least 1992, the party has emphasised unilateral <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_disarmament" title="Nuclear disarmament">nuclear disarmament</a> and called for the rejection of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Trident_nuclear_programme" title="Trident nuclear programme">Trident nuclear programme</a> of nuclear weapons in the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERootes199577_92-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERootes199577-92">[92]</a></sup> To campaign for the latter measure it has teamed up with the <a href="/wiki/Campaign_for_Nuclear_Disarmament" title="Campaign for Nuclear Disarmament">Campaign for Nuclear Disarmament</a>, <a href="/wiki/Plaid_Cymru" title="Plaid Cymru">Plaid Cymru</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Scottish_National_Party" title="Scottish National Party">Scottish National Party</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup> It wants to see the UK's Army turned into a <i>home defence force</i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup> and has pledged to take the UK out of <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">NATO</a> unilaterally.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup>
</p><p>The party has opposed <a href="/wiki/2003_invasion_of_Iraq" title="2003 invasion of Iraq">2003 invasion of Iraq</a>, NATO-led <a href="/wiki/2011_military_intervention_in_Libya" title="2011 military intervention in Libya">military intervention in Libya</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup> and British involvement in <a href="/wiki/Saudi_Arabian-led_intervention_in_Yemen" title="Saudi Arabian-led intervention in Yemen">Saudi Arabian-led intervention in Yemen</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup>
</p><p>The party campaigns for the rights of indigenous people and argues for greater <a href="/wiki/Autonomy" title="Autonomy">autonomy</a> for these individuals. Furthermore, they support the granting of compensation and justice for historical wrongs, and that the reappropriation of lands and resources should also take place. The party also believes that the cancelling of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/International_debt" title="International debt">international debt</a> should take place immediately and any financial assistance should be in the form of grants and not loans, limiting debt service payments to 10% of export earnings per year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gydg_86-1"><a href="#cite_note-gydg-86">[86]</a></sup>
</p><p>The party believes that environmental and social welfare should be prioritised over financial gain when it comes to regulating trade; a less "bully boy culture" from the  <a href="/wiki/Western_world" title="Western world">Western world</a> and more self sustainability in terms of food and energy policy on a global level, with aid only being given to countries as a last resort in order to prevent them from being indebted to their donors.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gydg_86-2"><a href="#cite_note-gydg-86">[86]</a></sup>
</p><p>Amid the toughening rhetoric surrounding immigration at the 2015 general election, the Greens issued mugs emblazoned with the slogan "Standing Up For Immigrants".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDennisonGoodwin2015184–185_98-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDennisonGoodwin2015184–185-98">[98]</a></sup> They claimed to offer a "genuine alternative" to the views of the mainstream parties by promoting the removal of restrictions on the number of foreign students, abolishing rules on family migration, and promoting further rights for asylum seekers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDennisonGoodwin2015185_85-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDennisonGoodwin2015185-85">[85]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Drug_policy">Drug policy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Green_Party_of_England_and_Wales&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Drug policy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The Green Party has an official "Drugs Group", for drugs policy and research,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup> and the party supports decriminalising the recreational use of <a href="/wiki/Cannabis" title="Cannabis">cannabis</a>, considering the drugs issue a health, rather than criminal issue.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup>
Ian Barnett from the Green Party says that: "The Policy of 'War on Drugs' has clearly failed. We need a different approach towards the control and misuse of drugs." However, the party does aim to minimise drug use due to the negative effects on the individual and society at large.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sexual_orientation_and_gender_identity">Sexual orientation and gender identity</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Green_Party_of_England_and_Wales&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Sexual orientation and gender identity">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The sexual orientation and gender identity group within the party known as LGBTIQA+ Greens stated aim is to <a href="/wiki/Consciousness_raising" title="Consciousness raising">raise awareness</a> on <a href="/wiki/LGBT_rights_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="LGBT rights in the United Kingdom">LGBTIQA+ rights</a> and issues affecting the broader <a href="/wiki/LGBT_community" title="LGBT community">LGBTIQA+ community</a>, as well as broader <a href="/wiki/Green_politics" title="Green politics">Green politics</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template noprint Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:No_original_research#Primary,_secondary_and_tertiary_sources" title="Wikipedia:No original research"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable secondary sources. (May 2018)">non-primary source needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p><p>The 2015 and 2017 general election manifestos contained policies on all teachers to be trained on LGBTIQA+ issues (such as "providing mandatory <a href="/wiki/HIV" title="HIV">HIV</a>, sex, and relationships education – age appropriate and LGBTIQA+-inclusive – in all schools from primary level onwards"), to reform the system of pensions, of end the "spousal veto"<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style#Technical_language" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style"><span title="The material near this tag may be using jargon that limits the article's accessibility. (May 2018)">jargon</span></a></i>]</sup> and to "make equal marriage truly equal".<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style#Technical_language" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style"><span title="The material near this tag may be using jargon that limits the article's accessibility. (May 2018)">jargon</span></a></i>]</sup> Bennett has also voiced support for <a href="/wiki/Polygamy" title="Polygamy">polygamy</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Polyamorous" title="Polyamorous">polyamorous</a> relationships.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup>
</p><p>The Green Party supports <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Same-sex_marriage_in_England_and_Wales" title="Same-sex marriage in England and Wales">same-sex marriage</a> and The Green Party group on <a href="/wiki/Brighton_and_Hove_City_Council" title="Brighton and Hove City Council">Brighton and Hove City Council</a> considered expelling a member (Christina Summers) in 2014 due to opposition to same-sex marriage legislation on religious grounds.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Governance">Governance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Green_Party_of_England_and_Wales&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Governance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Global_governance">Global governance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Green_Party_of_England_and_Wales&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Global governance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The party campaigns for greater accountability in global governance, with the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> made up of elected representatives and more regional representation, as opposed to the current nation-based setup. They want democratic control of the global economy with the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/World_Trade_Organisation" title="World Trade Organisation">World Trade Organisation</a>, <a href="/wiki/International_Monetary_Fund" title="International Monetary Fund">International Monetary Fund</a> and <a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">World Bank</a> reformed, democratised or even replaced. The party also wishes to prioritise social and environmental sustainability as a global policy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gydg_86-3"><a href="#cite_note-gydg-86">[86]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="National_governance">National governance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Green_Party_of_England_and_Wales&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: National governance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The party advocates ending the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/First_past_the_post_voting" title="First past the post voting">first past the post voting</a> system for UK parliamentary elections and replacing it with a form of <a href="/wiki/Proportional_representation" title="Proportional representation">proportional representation</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBirch200965_105-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBirch200965-105">[105]</a></sup>
</p><p>The Green Party states that they believe there is "no place in government for the hereditary principle",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup> while Bennett has said that she supports the abolition of the monarchy as the head of state, and fully supports <a href="/wiki/Republicanism_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="Republicanism in the United Kingdom">replacing the monarchy with a republic</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="European_Union">European Union</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Green_Party_of_England_and_Wales&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: European Union">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The party supported <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_European_Union_membership_referendum,_2016" title="United Kingdom European Union membership referendum, 2016">the 2016 referendum</a> on the United Kingdom's membership of the European Union, calling it "a vital opportunity to create a more democratic and accountable Europe, with a clearer purpose for the future".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template noprint Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:No_original_research#Primary,_secondary_and_tertiary_sources" title="Wikipedia:No original research"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable secondary sources. (May 2018)">non-primary source needed</span></a></i>]</sup> The party has criticised the <a href="/wiki/Common_Agricultural_Policy" title="Common Agricultural Policy">Common Agricultural Policy</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Common_Fisheries_Policy" title="Common Fisheries Policy">Common Fisheries Policy</a> and the "excessive influence" of the <a href="/wiki/European_Commission" title="European Commission">European Commission</a> in comparison to the <a href="/wiki/European_Council" title="European Council">European Council</a> and <a href="/wiki/European_Parliament" title="European Parliament">European Parliament</a>, describing it as "undemocratic and unaccountable".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Europe_policy_109-0"><a href="#cite_note-Europe_policy-109">[109]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template noprint Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:No_original_research#Primary,_secondary_and_tertiary_sources" title="Wikipedia:No original research"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable secondary sources. (May 2018)">non-primary source needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
The party favoured a "three yeses" approach to Europe: "yes to a referendum, yes to major EU reform and yes to staying in a reformed Europe". Bennett also added that:
</p>
<blockquote><p>'Yes to the EU' does not mean we are content with the union continuing to operate as it has in the past. There is a huge democratic deficit in its functioning, a serious bias towards the interests of neoliberalism and 'the market', and central institutions have been overbuilt. But to achieve those reforms we need to work with fellow EU members, not try to dictate high handedly to them, as David Cameron has done.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup></p></blockquote>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Young_Greens">Young Greens</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Green_Party_of_England_and_Wales&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Young Greens">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Young_Greens_of_England_and_Wales" title="Young Greens of England and Wales">Young Greens of England and Wales</a></div>
<p>The youth wing of the Green Party, the Young Greens (of England and Wales), has developed independently from around 2002, and is for all Green Party members aged up to 30 years old. There is no lower age limit. The Young Greens have their own constitution, national committee, campaigns and meetings, and have become an active presence at Green Party Conferences and election campaigns. There are now many Young Greens groups on UK university, college and higher-education institution campuses. Many Green Party councillors are Young Greens, as are some members of GPEx and other internal party organs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-YGSite1_111-0"><a href="#cite_note-YGSite1-111">[111]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Membership_and_finances">Membership and finances</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Green_Party_of_England_and_Wales&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Membership and finances">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Update" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><img alt="Ambox current red.svg" data-file-height="290" data-file-width="360" height="34" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Ambox_current_red.svg/42px-Ambox_current_red.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Ambox_current_red.svg/63px-Ambox_current_red.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Ambox_current_red.svg/84px-Ambox_current_red.svg.png 2x" width="42"/></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section needs to be <b>updated</b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please update this article to reflect recent events or newly available information.</span> <small><i>(May 2018)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>According to accounts filed with the <a href="/wiki/Electoral_Commission_(United_Kingdom)" title="Electoral Commission (United Kingdom)">Electoral Commission</a>, for the year ending 31 December 2010 the party had an income of £770,495 with expenditure of £889,867.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-soa-2010_112-0"><a href="#cite_note-soa-2010-112">[112]</a></sup>
Membership increased rapidly in 2014, more than doubling in that year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-greenparty.org.uk_113-0"><a href="#cite_note-greenparty.org.uk-113">[113]</a></sup> On 15 January 2015, the Green Party claimed that the combined membership of the UK Green parties (Green Party of England and Wales, <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Green_Party" title="Scottish Green Party">Scottish Green Party</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Green_Party_in_Northern_Ireland" title="Green Party in Northern Ireland">Green Party in Northern Ireland</a>) had risen to 43,829 members, surpassing <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UKIP" title="UKIP">UKIP</a>'s membership of 41,966, and making it the third-largest UK-wide political party in the UK in terms of membership.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBC_News_15_January_2015_114-0"><a href="#cite_note-BBC_News_15_January_2015-114">[114]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-The_Independent_15_January_2015_115-0"><a href="#cite_note-The_Independent_15_January_2015-115">[115]</a></sup> On 14 January 2015, UK newspaper <i>The Guardian</i> had reported that membership of the combined UK Green Parties was closing on those of UKIP and the Liberal Democrats, but noted that it lagged behind that of the <a href="/wiki/Scottish_National_Party" title="Scottish National Party">Scottish National Party</a> (SNP), which has a membership of 92,187 members but is not a UK-wide party.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-The_Guardian_14_January_2015_116-0"><a href="#cite_note-The_Guardian_14_January_2015-116">[116]</a></sup> Membership of the party peaked at over 67,000 members in the summer of 2015 after the general election, but has since declined subsequent to Jeremy Corbyn becoming leader of the Labour Party.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup>
</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Support_base">Support base</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Green_Party_of_England_and_Wales&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Support base">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="quotebox pullquote floatright" style="width:25em; ;"><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r856303512">.mw-parser-output .quotebox{background-color:#F9F9F9;border:1px solid #aaa;box-sizing:border-box;padding:10px;font-size:88%}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatleft{margin:0.5em 1.4em 0.8em 0}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatright{margin:0.5em 0 0.8em 1.4em}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.centered{margin:0.5em auto 0.8em auto}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatleft p,.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatright p{font-style:inherit}.mw-parser-output .quotebox-title{background-color:#F9F9F9;text-align:center;font-size:larger;font-weight:bold}.mw-parser-output .quotebox-quote.quoted:before{font-family:"Times New Roman",serif;font-weight:bold;font-size:large;color:gray;content:" “ ";vertical-align:-45%;line-height:0}.mw-parser-output .quotebox-quote.quoted:after{font-family:"Times New Roman",serif;font-weight:bold;font-size:large;color:gray;content:" ” ";line-height:0}.mw-parser-output .quotebox .left-aligned{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .quotebox .right-aligned{text-align:right}.mw-parser-output .quotebox .center-aligned{text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .quotebox cite{display:block;font-style:normal}@media screen and (max-width:360px){.mw-parser-output .quotebox{min-width:100%;margin:0 0 0.8em!important;float:none!important}}</style>
<div class="quotebox-quote left-aligned" style="">"Green voters have tended to be younger and better educated than the electorate at large, and they are known to be more likely than most voters to work in the <a href="/wiki/Public_sector" title="Public sector">public sector</a>. In terms of values, Green voters have been found to be more often than not on the left of the political spectrum, and they have been more likely than the average voter to hold <a href="/wiki/Post-materialism" title="Post-materialism">post-materialist</a> values, including support for environmental protection."</div>
<p><cite class="left-aligned" style="">— Sarah Birch, 2009<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBirch200961_132-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBirch200961-132">[132]</a></sup></cite>
</p>
</div>
<p>According to political scientist <a href="/wiki/Sarah_Birch" title="Sarah Birch">Sarah Birch</a>, the Green Party draws support from "a wide spectrum of the population".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBirch200953_133-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBirch200953-133">[133]</a></sup>
In 1995, sociologist <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Chris_Rootes&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Chris Rootes (page does not exist)">Chris Rootes</a> stated that the Green Party "appeals disproportionately to younger, highly educated professional people" although noted that this support base was "not predominantly urban".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERootes199585_134-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERootes199585-134">[134]</a></sup>
In 2009, Birch noted that the Green's strongest areas of support were Labour-held seats in university towns or urban areas with relatively large student populations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBirch200958&amp;ndash;59_135-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBirch200958&amp;ndash;59-135">[135]</a></sup> She noted that there were also strong correlations between areas of high Green support and high percentages of people who define themselves as having <a href="/wiki/Irreligion" title="Irreligion">no religion</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBirch200959&amp;ndash;60_136-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBirch200959&amp;ndash;60-136">[136]</a></sup>
</p><p>Birch noted that sociological polling revealed a "strong relationship" between individuals having voted for the <a href="/wiki/Liberal_Democrats_(UK)" title="Liberal Democrats (UK)">Liberal Democrats</a> in the past and holding favourable views of the Green Party, noting that the two groups were competing for "similar sorts of voters".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBirch200964_137-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBirch200964-137">[137]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Electoral_representation">Electoral representation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Green_Party_of_England_and_Wales&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Electoral representation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Green_Party_of_England_and_Wales_election_results" title="Green Party of England and Wales election results">Green Party of England and Wales election results</a></div>
<table align="right">
<tbody><tr>
