<p>The party has one <a href="/wiki/House_of_Commons_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="House of Commons of the United Kingdom">Member of Parliament</a>, one member of the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Lords" title="House of Lords">House of Lords</a>, three Members of the <a href="/wiki/European_Parliament" title="European Parliament">European Parliament</a> and two Members of the <a href="/wiki/London_Assembly" title="London Assembly">London Assembly</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-138"><a href="#cite_note-138">[138]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-139"><a href="#cite_note-139">[139]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="House_of_Commons">House of Commons</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Green_Party_of_England_and_Wales&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: House of Commons">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Brighton_Pavilion_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="Brighton Pavilion (UK Parliament constituency)">Brighton Pavilion</a> was the Green Party's first and only parliamentary seat to date, won at the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_general_election,_2010" title="United Kingdom general election, 2010">2010 general election</a> and held in <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_general_election,_2015" title="United Kingdom general election, 2015">2015</a> and <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_general_election,_2017" title="United Kingdom general election, 2017">2017</a>. As with other small parties, representation at the House of Commons has been hindered by the <a href="/wiki/First-past-the-post_voting" title="First-past-the-post voting">first-past-the-post</a> voting system.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERootes199568Birch200956,_65_140-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERootes199568Birch200956,_65-140">[140]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="House_of_Lords">House of Lords</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Green_Party_of_England_and_Wales&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: House of Lords">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The party's first <a href="/wiki/Life_peer" title="Life peer">life peer</a> was <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Baron_Beaumont_of_Whitley" title="Baron Beaumont of Whitley">Baron Beaumont of Whitley</a>, who left the Liberal Democrats and joined the Green Party in 1999. He sat as a Green until his death in 2008.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBirch200966_141-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBirch200966-141">[141]</a></sup> As of December 2015, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Baroness_Jones_of_Moulsecoomb" title="Baroness Jones of Moulsecoomb">Baroness Jones of Moulsecoomb</a> is their only representative in the House of Lords.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-auto_142-0"><a href="#cite_note-auto-142">[142]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="European_Parliament">European Parliament</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Green_Party_of_England_and_Wales&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: European Parliament">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Since the first UK election to the European Parliament with proportional representation, in 1999, the Green Party of England and Wales has had representation in the European Parliament.  From 1999 to 2010, the two MEPs were <a href="/wiki/Jean_Lambert" title="Jean Lambert">Jean Lambert</a> (London) and Lucas (South East England).  In 2010, on election to the House of Commons, Lucas resigned her seat and was succeeded by <a href="/wiki/Keith_Taylor_(British_politician)" title="Keith Taylor (British politician)">Keith Taylor</a>.  In 2014, Taylor and Lambert held their seats, and were joined by <a href="/wiki/Molly_Scott_Cato" title="Molly Scott Cato">Molly Scott Cato</a> who was elected in the South West region, increasing the number of Green Party Members of the European Parliament to three for the first time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-143"><a href="#cite_note-143">[143]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Local_government">Local government</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Green_Party_of_England_and_Wales&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Local government">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>From the early 1990s until 2009, the number of Green local councillors rose from zero to over 100.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBirch200956_42-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBirch200956-42">[42]</a></sup>
</p><p>The party has representation at <a href="/wiki/Local_government_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="Local government in the United Kingdom">local government level</a> in England. The party has limited representation on most councils on which it is represented, and was in <a href="/wiki/Minority_government" title="Minority government">minority control</a> of <a href="/wiki/Brighton_and_Hove_City_Council" title="Brighton and Hove City Council">Brighton and Hove City Council</a> from <a href="/wiki/Brighton_and_Hove_City_Council_election,_2011" title="Brighton and Hove City Council election, 2011">2011</a> to <a href="/wiki/Brighton_and_Hove_City_Council_election,_2015" title="Brighton and Hove City Council election, 2015">2015</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-144"><a href="#cite_note-144">[144]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-145"><a href="#cite_note-145">[145]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Wales_Green_Party">Wales Green Party</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Green_Party_of_England_and_Wales&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Wales Green Party">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Wales_Green_Party" title="Wales Green Party">Wales Green Party</a></div>
<p>The Wales Green Party (WGP; <a href="/wiki/Welsh_language" title="Welsh language">Welsh</a>: <i lang="cy">Plaid Werdd Cymru</i>) is a semi-<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Autonomous_entity" title="Autonomous entity">autonomous</a> <a href="/wiki/Political_party" title="Political party">political party</a> within the Green Party of England and Wales. It covers <a href="/wiki/Wales" title="Wales">Wales</a>, and is the only regional party with autonomous status within the GPEW. The WGP contests elections for the <a href="/wiki/National_Assembly_for_Wales" title="National Assembly for Wales">National Assembly for Wales</a> (as well as at the <a href="/wiki/Local_government_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="Local government in the United Kingdom">local</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UK_Parliament" title="UK Parliament">UK</a> and <a href="/wiki/European_Parliament" title="European Parliament">European</a> level) and has its own newsletters, membership list, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Annual_General_Meeting" title="Annual General Meeting">AGMs</a> and <a href="/wiki/Manifesto" title="Manifesto">manifesto</a>. Members of the WGP are automatically members of the GPEW. The WGP leader is Grenville Ham,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WGPSite1_146-0"><a href="#cite_note-WGPSite1-146">[146]</a></sup> and the Deputy Leaders are Benjamin Smith and Pippa Bartolotti.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-147"><a href="#cite_note-147">[147]</a></sup> Wales is represented internally within the GPEW by Chris Simpson and Chris Carmichael on the Green Party Regional Council.  Both sets of positions are directly elected by postal ballot. Wales-wide decisions are taken by the Wales Green Party Council made up of the spokespeople, senior officers, and a representative from each local party.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Leadership">Leadership</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Green_Party_of_England_and_Wales&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Leadership">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The party leader from December 2015 until her resignation in March 2017 was Alice Hooker-Stroud;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-148"><a href="#cite_note-148">[148]</a></sup> the current Leader is <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Grenville_Ham&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Grenville Ham (page does not exist)">Grenville Ham</a>, and the current Deputy Leaders are Benjamin Smith and Pippa Bartolotti.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-149"><a href="#cite_note-149">[149]</a></sup> Wales is represented internally within the GPEW by Chris Simpson and Chris Carmichael on the <a href="/wiki/Green_Party_of_England_and_Wales#Regional_Council" title="Green Party of England and Wales">Green Party Regional Council</a> (GPRC).  Both sets of positions are directly elected by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Postal_ballot" title="Postal ballot">postal ballot</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="History_2">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Green_Party_of_England_and_Wales&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The Green Parties in the United Kingdom have their roots in the PEOPLE movement which was founded in 1972. This became the Ecology Party three years later, and then the <a href="/wiki/Green_Party_(UK)" title="Green Party (UK)">Green Party</a> in 1985. Scotland, Wales and Northern Ireland each had separate branches. In 1990, the Scottish and Northern Irish branches left the UK Greens to form separate parties. The English and Welsh parties became the Green Party of England and Wales, with the Welsh branch being semi-autonomous.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-150"><a href="#cite_note-150">[150]</a></sup> At the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_general_election,_1992" title="United Kingdom general election, 1992">1992 general election</a>, local Greens entered an electoral alliance with <a href="/wiki/Plaid_Cymru" title="Plaid Cymru">Plaid Cymru</a> in the constituency of <a href="/wiki/Ceredigion_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="Ceredigion (UK Parliament constituency)">Ceredigion and Pembroke North</a>. The alliance was successful with <a href="/wiki/Cynog_Dafis" title="Cynog Dafis">Cynog Dafis</a> being returned in a surprise result as the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Member_of_Parliament" title="Member of Parliament">MP</a>, defeating the <a href="/wiki/Liberal_Democrats_(UK)" title="Liberal Democrats (UK)">Liberal Democrat</a> incumbent by over 3,000 votes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-151"><a href="#cite_note-151">[151]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-152"><a href="#cite_note-152">[152]</a></sup> The agreement broke down by 1995 following disagreement within the Welsh Green Party over endorsing another party's candidate, though Dafis would go on to serve in parliament as a Plaid Cymru member until 2000, and in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_Assembly_of_Wales" title="National Assembly of Wales">National Assembly of Wales</a> from 1999 until 2003. Dafis later stated that he did not consider himself to be the "first Green MP".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-153"><a href="#cite_note-153">[153]</a></sup>
</p><p>The Wales Green Party has always had its own spokesperson (now referred to as leader). Jake Griffiths became leader in 2009.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-154"><a href="#cite_note-154">[154]</a></sup> Pippa Bartolotti was elected to succeed him in 2011, followed by Alice Hooker-Stroud.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-155"><a href="#cite_note-155">[155]</a></sup> Anthony Slaughter became deputy leader in 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-156"><a href="#cite_note-156">[156]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Elections">Elections</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Green_Party_of_England_and_Wales&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Elections">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
